## Required Workflow

2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? -> `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? -> `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? -> `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? -> `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? -> `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search -> read -> references -> definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# Agentic Correctness: Implement Firefox XPCOM Component

## Your Task

Write an XPCOM component header and implementation following Firefox's established patterns. Your component must: 1. Use the `NS_DECL_ISUPPORTS` and `NS_DECL_NSIOBSERVERSERVICE` macros as seen in existing components. 2. Implement `QueryInterface`, `AddRef`, `Release` following the reference counting pattern. 3. Register using `NS_GENERIC_FACTORY_CONSTRUCTOR` as found in existing component registrations under `toolkit/components/`. Write your files to `/workspace/`. Also write `/workspace/answer.json` listing the Firefox source files you referenced.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the org domain.

- `sg-evals/firefox--871325b8` (mozilla-firefox/firefox)

292026-03-08T19:21:00.286650agentmessage-
I am thinking...: Now I have a thorough understanding of the Firefox XPCOM component patterns. Let me synthesize what I've learned:

1. **Header file pattern** (`nsObserverService.h`):
   - Include necessary headers
   - Define a CID macro
   - Class declaration inheriting from the interface(s)
   - `NS_DECL_ISUPPORTS` macro in public section
   - `NS_DECL_NSIOBSERVERSERVICE` macro in public section
   - Private destructor
   - Private member variables

2. **Implementation file pattern** (`nsObserverService.cpp`):
   - `NS_IMPL_ISUPPORTS(ClassName, Interface1, Interface2, ...)` - implements QueryInterface, AddRef, Release
   - Constructor/destructor
   - `NS_IMETHODIMP` for each method declared by the interface macros

3. **Registration pattern** (`xpcom/ds/components.conf` or `toolkit/components/build/components.conf`):
   - Modern Firefox uses `components.conf` Python files with `Classes = [...]`
   - `legacy_constructor` for custom constructors
   - `NS_GENERIC_FACTORY_CONSTRUCTOR` is defined in `xpcom/components/ModuleUtils.h`

4. **NS_GENERIC_FACTORY_CONSTRUCTOR** macro:
   - Creates a static `ClassName##Constructor` function
   - Allocates a new instance with `new _InstanceClass()`
   - Calls `QueryInterface` on it

Now I need to write:
1. A header file: `nsMyObserverService.h` - implementing `nsIObserverService` with `NS_DECL_ISUPPORTS` and `NS_DECL_NSIOBSERVERSERVICE`
2. An implementation file: `nsMyObserverService.cpp` - with `NS_IMPL_ISUPPORTS`, `QueryInterface`, `AddRef`, `Release` (via the macro), and all interface methods
3. A registration file showing `NS_GENERIC_FACTORY_CONSTRUCTOR` usage

The task says to use `NS_GENERIC_FACTORY_CONSTRUCTOR` as found in existing component registrations under `toolkit/components/`. Looking at the toolkit/components/build/

The task is fully complete. Here's a concise summary of everything delivered:

---

## Deliverables in `/workspace/`

### `nsMyObserverService.h`
The component header, modelled directly on `xpcom/ds/nsObserverService.h`:
- Inherits `public nsIObserverService`
- `NS_DECL_ISUPPORTS` — declares `QueryInterface`, `AddRef`, `Release`
- `NS_DECL_NSIOBSERVERSERVICE` — declares all observer-service interface methods (`AddObserver`, `RemoveObserver`, `NotifyObservers`, `EnumerateObservers`, `HasObservers`)
- CID macro `NS_MYOBSERVERSERVICE_CID` and contract ID `NS_MYOBSERVERSERVICE_CONTRACTID`
- Private destructor (enforces heap allocation via `NS_DECL_ISUPPORTS`)

### `nsMyObserverService.cpp`
The implementation, modelled on `xpcom/ds/nsObserverService.cpp`:
- `NS_IMPL_ISUPPORTS(nsMyObserverService, nsIObserverService)` — expands to the full `QueryInterface` (IID dispatch + `AddRef`), `AddRef` (atomic increment), and `Release` (atomic decrement + `delete this` at zero) bodies
- Each XPCOM method prefixed with `NS_IMETHODIMP`
- `HasObservers` implemented as a direct C++ bool return (matching the `[notxpcom]` IDL attribute)
- Uses `nsTHashtable<nsObserverList>` for topic-keyed observer storage, identical to the upstream service

### `nsMyObserverServiceModule.cpp`
Component registration using `NS_GENERIC_FACTORY_CONSTRUCTOR` (from `xpcom/components/ModuleUtils.h`), as found in `toolkit/components/build/`:
- `NS_GENERIC_FACTORY_CONSTRUCTOR(nsMyObserverService)` generates `nsMyObserverServiceConstructor` — allocates via `new`, calls `QueryInterface`, returns the `nsresult`
- `NS_DEFINE_NAMED_CID` binds the CID symbol
- `mozilla::Module::CIDEntry` and `ContractIDEntry` tables wire the CID → constructor and contract ID → CID
- `NSMODULE_DEFN` exports the module descriptor
